  3 15    Sec. 7.    3 15    Sec. 7.    3 16    As used in this chapter, unless the context otherwise
  3 17 requires:
  3 18    1.  "Board" means the board of respiratory care and
  3 19 polysomnography established in chapter 147.
  3 20    2.  "Direct supervision" means that the polysomnographic
  3 21 technologist providing supervision must be present where the
  3 22 polysomnographic procedure is being performed and immediately
  3 23 available to furnish assistance and direction throughout the
  3 24 performance of the procedure.
  3 25    3.  "General supervision" means that the polysomnographic
  3 26 procedure is provided under a physician's or qualified health
  3 27 care professional prescriber's overall direction and control,
  3 28 but the physician's or qualified health care professional
  3 29 prescriber's presence is not required during the performance
  3 30 of the procedure.
  3 31    4.  "Physician" means a person who is currently licensed in
  3 32 Iowa to practice medicine and surgery or osteopathic medicine
  3 33 and surgery and who is board certified and who is actively
  3 34 involved in the sleep medicine center or laboratory.
  3 35    5.  "Polysomnographic student" means a person who is
  4  1 enrolled in a program approved by the board and who may
  4  2 provide sleep=related services under the direct supervision
  4  3 of a polysomnographic technologist as a part of the person's
  4  4 educational program.
  4  5    6.  "Polysomnographic technician" means a person who has
  4  6 graduated from a program approved by the board, but has not
  4  7 yet received an accepted national credential awarded from an
  4  8 examination program approved by the board and who may provide
  4  9 sleep=related services under the direct supervision of a
  4 10 licensed polysomnographic technologist for a period of up to
  4 11 thirty days following graduation while awaiting credentialing
  4 12 examination scheduling and results.
  4 13    7.  "Polysomnographic technologist" means a person licensed
  4 14 by the board to engage in the practice of polysomnography under
  4 15 the general supervision of a physician or a qualified health
  4 16 care professional prescriber.
  4 17    8.  "Practice of polysomnography" means as described in
  4 18 section 148G.2.
  4 19    9.  "Qualified health care practitioner" means an individual
  4 20 who is licensed under section 147.2, and who holds a
  4 21 credential listed on the board of registered polysomnographic
  4 22 technologists list of accepted allied health credentials.
  4 23    10.  "Qualified health care professional prescriber" means a
  4 24 physician assistant operating under the prescribing authority
  4 25 granted in section 147.107 or an advanced registered nurse
  4 26 practitioner operating under the prescribing authority granted
  4 27 in section 147.107.
  4 28    11.  "Sleep=related services" means acts performed by
  4 29 polysomnographic technicians, polysomnographic students, and
  4 30 other persons permitted to perform those services under this
  4 31 chapter, in a setting described in this chapter that would be
  4 32 considered the practice of polysomnography if performed by a
  4 33 polysomnographic technologist.

  4  3 of a polysomnographic technologist as a part of the person's
  4  4 educational program.
  4  5    6.  "Polysomnographic technician" means a person who has
  4  6 graduated from a program approved by the board, but has not
  4  7 yet received an accepted national credential awarded from an
  4  8 examination program approved by the board and who may provide
  4  9 sleep=related services under the direct supervision of a
  4 10 licensed polysomnographic technologist for a period of up to
  4 11 thirty days following graduation while awaiting credentialing
  4 12 examination scheduling and results.
  4 13    7.  "Polysomnographic technologist" means a person licensed
  4 14 by the board to engage in the practice of polysomnography under
  4 15 the general supervision of a physician or a qualified health
  4 16 care professional prescriber.
  4 17    8.  "Practice of polysomnography" means as described in
  4 18 section 148G.2.
  4 19    9.  "Qualified health care practitioner" means an individual
  4 20 who is licensed under section 147.2, and who holds a
  4 21 credential listed on the board of registered polysomnographic
  4 22 technologists list of accepted allied health credentials.
  4 23    10.  "Qualified health care professional prescriber" means a
  4 24 physician assistant operating under the prescribing authority
  4 25 granted in section 147.107 or an advanced registered nurse
  4 26 practitioner operating under the prescribing authority granted
  4 27 in section 147.107.

  4 31 chapter, in a setting described in this chapter that would be
  4 32 considered the practice of polysomnography if performed by a

  4 34    Sec. 8.    4 34    Sec. 8.    4 35    The practice of polysomnography consists of but is not
  5  1 limited to the following tasks as performed for the purpose of
  5  2 polysomnography, under the general supervision of a licensed
  5  3 physician or qualified health care professional prescriber:
  5  4    1.  Monitoring, recording, and evaluating physiologic
  5  5 data during polysomnographic testing and review during the
  5  6 evaluation of sleep=related disorders, including sleep=related
  5  7 respiratory disturbances, by applying any of the following
  5  8 techniques, equipment, or procedures:
  5  9    a.  Noninvasive continuous, bilevel positive airway pressure,
  5 10 or adaptive servo=ventilation titration on spontaneously
  5 11 breathing patients using a mask or oral appliance; provided,
  5 12 that the mask or oral appliance does not extend into the
  5 13 trachea or attach to an artificial airway.
  5 14    b.  Supplemental low=flow oxygen therapy of less than six
  5 15 liters per minute, utilizing a nasal cannula or incorporated
  5 16 into a positive airway pressure device during a polysomnogram.
  5 17    c.  Capnography during a polysomnogram.
  5 18    d.  Cardiopulmonary resuscitation.
  5 19    e.  Pulse oximetry.
  5 20    f.  Gastroesophageal pH monitoring.
  5 21    g.  Esophageal pressure monitoring.
  5 22    h.  Sleep stage recording using surface
  5 23 electroencephalography, surface electrooculography, and surface
  5 24 submental electromyography.
  5 25    i.  Surface electromyography.
  5 26    j.  Electrocardiography.
  5 27    k.  Respiratory effort monitoring, including thoracic and
  5 28 abdominal movement.
  5 29    l.  Plethysmography blood flow monitoring.
  5 30    m.  Snore monitoring.
  5 31    n.  Audio and video monitoring.
  5 32    o.  Body movement monitoring.
  5 33    p.  Nocturnal penile tumescence monitoring.
  5 34    q.  Nasal and oral airflow monitoring.
  5 35    r.  Body temperature monitoring.
  6  1    2.  Monitoring the effects that a mask or oral appliance
  6  2 used to treat sleep disorders has on sleep patterns; provided,
  6  3 however, that the mask or oral appliance shall not extend into
  6  4 the trachea or attach to an artificial airway.
  6  5    3.  Observing and monitoring physical signs and symptoms,
  6  6 general behavior, and general physical response to
  6  7 polysomnographic evaluation and determining whether initiation,
  6  8 modification, or discontinuation of a treatment regimen is
  6  9 warranted.
  6 10    4.  Analyzing and scoring data collected during the
  6 11 monitoring described in this section for the purpose of
  6 12 assisting a physician in the diagnosis and treatment of sleep
  6 13 and wake disorders that result from developmental defects,
  6 14 the aging process, physical injury, disease, or actual or
  6 15 anticipated somatic dysfunction.
  6 16    5.  Implementation of a written or verbal order from a
  6 17 physician or qualified health care professional prescriber to
  6 18 perform polysomnography.
  6 19    6.  Education of a patient regarding the treatment regimen
  6 20 that assists the patient in improving the patient's sleep.
  6 21    7.  Use of any oral appliance used to treat sleep=disordered
  6 22 breathing while under the care of a licensed polysomnographic
  6 23 technologist during the performance of a sleep study, as
  6 24 directed by a licensed dentist.

  6 27 facility that is accredited by a nationally recognized sleep
  6 28 medicine laboratory or center accrediting agency, in a facility
  6 29 operated by a hospital or a hospital licensed under chapter
  6 30 135B, or in a patient's home pursuant to rules adopted by the
  6 31 board; provided, however, that the scoring of data and the
  6 32 education of patients may take place in another setting.

  7  5 and administration of this chapter and the applicable
  7  6 provisions of chapters 147 and 272C.
  7  7    Sec. 12.    7  5 and administration of this chapter and the applicable
  7  6 provisions of chapters 147 and 272C.
  7  7    Sec. 12.    7  6 provisions of chapters 147 and 272C.
  7  7    Sec. 12.    7  7    Sec. 12.    7  8    1.  Beginning January 1, 2017, a person seeking licensure
  7  9 as a polysomnographic technologist shall apply to the board
  7 10 and pay the fees established by the board for licensure.
  7 11 The application shall show that the applicant is of good
  7 12 moral character and is at least eighteen years of age, and
  7 13 shall include proof that the person has satisfied one of the
  7 14 following educational requirements:
  7 15    a.  Graduation from a polysomnographic educational program
  7 16 that is accredited by the committee on accreditation for
  7 17 polysomnographic technologist education or an equivalent
  7 18 program as determined by the board.
  7 19    b.  Graduation from a respiratory care educational program
  7 20 that is accredited by the commission on accreditation for
  7 21 respiratory care or by a committee on accreditation for
  7 22 the commission on accreditation of allied health education
  7 23 programs, and any of the following:
  7 24    (1)  Completion of the curriculum for a polysomnographic
  7 25 certificate established and accredited by the commission
  7 26 on accreditation of allied health education programs as an
  7 27 extension of the respiratory care program.
  7 28    (2)  Obtaining the sleep disorder specialist credential from
  7 29 the national board for respiratory care.
  7 30    (3)  Obtaining the registered polysomnographic technologist
  7 31 credential from the board of registered polysomnographic
  7 32 technologists.
  7 33    (4)  Completing or obtaining any other certificate or
  7 34 credential program as recognized by the board.
  7 35    c.  Graduation from an electroneurodiagnostic technologist
  8  1 educational program that is accredited by the committee
  8  2 on accreditation for education in electroneurodiagnostic
  8  3 technology or by a committee on accreditation for the
  8  4 commission on accreditation of allied health education
  8  5 programs, and completion of the curriculum for a
  8  6 polysomnographic certificate established and accredited by the
  8  7 commission on accreditation of allied health education programs
  8  8 as an extension of the electroneurodiagnostic educational
  8  9 program.
  8 10    2.  a.  Notwithstanding subsection 1, beginning January
  8 11 1, 2017, the board shall issue a license to perform
  8 12 polysomnography to an individual who holds an active license
  8 13 under section 147.2 in a profession other than polysomnography
  8 14 and who is in good standing with the board for that profession
  8 15 upon application to the board demonstrating any of the
  8 16 following:
  8 17    (1)  Successful completion of an educational program in
  8 18 polysomnography approved by the board.
  8 19    (2)  Successful completion of an examination in
  8 20 polysomnography approved by the board.
  8 21    (3)  Verification from the medical director of the
  8 22 individual's current employer or the medical director's
  8 23 designee that the individual has completed on=the=job
  8 24 training in the field of polysomnography as approved by
  8 25 the board, along with written verification from the medical
  8 26 director of the individual's current employer or the medical
  8 27 director's designee that the individual is competent to perform
  8 28 polysomnography.
  8 29    b.  The board shall not collect a licensing or application
  8 30 fee from a health care practitioner who receives a license
  8 31 pursuant to this subsection.
  8 32    3.  Notwithstanding subsection 1, beginning January 1,
  8 33 2017, a person who is working in the field of sleep medicine
  8 34 on January 1, 2017, may apply to the board for a license to
  8 35 perform polysomnography. The board shall issue a license to
  9  1 the person, without examination, provided the application
  9  2 contains verification that the person has completed five
  9  3 hundred hours of paid clinical or nonclinical polysomnographic
  9  4 work experience within the three years prior to submission
  9  5 of the application. The application shall also contain
  9  6 verification from the medical director of the person's current
  9  7 employer or the medical director's designee that the person
  9  8 is competent to perform polysomnography. An active license
  9  9 holder under section 147.2 being issued a license under this
  9 10 subsection is exempt from paying the licensure fee required for
  9 11 a polysomnography license.
  9 12    4.  A person who is working in the field of sleep medicine
  9 13 on January 1, 2017, who is not otherwise eligible to obtain
  9 14 a license pursuant to this section shall have until January
  9 15 1, 2018, to achieve a passing score on an examination as
  9 16 designated by the board. The board shall allow the person
  9 17 to attempt the examination and be awarded a license as a
  9 18 polysomnographic technologist by meeting or exceeding the
  9 19 passing point established by the board. After January 1,
  9 20 2018, only persons licensed as polysomnographic technologists
  9 21 pursuant to this chapter, or excepted from the requirements of
  9 22 this chapter may perform sleep=related services.
  9 23    5.  The fees assessed by the board shall be sufficient to
  9 24 cover all costs associated with the administration of this
  9 25 chapter.
  9 26    Sec. 13.    7  9 as a polysomnographic technologist shall apply to the board
  7 10 and pay the fees established by the board for licensure.
  7 11 The application shall show that the applicant is of good
  7 12 moral character and is at least eighteen years of age, and
  7 13 shall include proof that the person has satisfied one of the
  7 14 following educational requirements:
  7 15    a.  Graduation from a polysomnographic educational program
  7 16 that is accredited by the committee on accreditation for
  7 17 polysomnographic technologist education or an equivalent
  7 18 program as determined by the board.
  7 19    b.  Graduation from a respiratory care educational program
  7 20 that is accredited by the commission on accreditation for
  7 21 respiratory care or by a committee on accreditation for
  7 22 the commission on accreditation of allied health education
  7 23 programs, and any of the following:
  7 24    (1)  Completion of the curriculum for a polysomnographic
  7 25 certificate established and accredited by the commission
  7 26 on accreditation of allied health education programs as an
  7 27 extension of the respiratory care program.
  7 28    (2)  Obtaining the sleep disorder specialist credential from
  7 29 the national board for respiratory care.
  7 30    (3)  Obtaining the registered polysomnographic technologist
  7 31 credential from the board of registered polysomnographic
  7 32 technologists.
  7 33    (4)  Completing or obtaining any other certificate or
  7 34 credential program as recognized by the board.
  7 35    c.  Graduation from an electroneurodiagnostic technologist
  8  1 educational program that is accredited by the committee
  8  2 on accreditation for education in electroneurodiagnostic
  8  3 technology or by a committee on accreditation for the
  8  4 commission on accreditation of allied health education
  8  5 programs, and completion of the curriculum for a
  8  6 polysomnographic certificate established and accredited by the
  8  7 commission on accreditation of allied health education programs
  8  8 as an extension of the electroneurodiagnostic educational
  8  9 program.
  8 10    2.  a.  Notwithstanding subsection 1, beginning January
  8 11 1, 2017, the board shall issue a license to perform
  8 12 polysomnography to an individual who holds an active license
  8 13 under section 147.2 in a profession other than polysomnography
  8 14 and who is in good standing with the board for that profession
  8 15 upon application to the board demonstrating any of the
  8 16 following:
  8 17    (1)  Successful completion of an educational program in
  8 18 polysomnography approved by the board.
  8 19    (2)  Successful completion of an examination in
  8 20 polysomnography approved by the board.
  8 21    (3)  Verification from the medical director of the
  8 22 individual's current employer or the medical director's
  8 23 designee that the individual has completed on=the=job
  8 24 training in the field of polysomnography as approved by
  8 25 the board, along with written verification from the medical
  8 26 director of the individual's current employer or the medical
  8 27 director's designee that the individual is competent to perform
  8 28 polysomnography.
  8 29    b.  The board shall not collect a licensing or application
  8 30 fee from a health care practitioner who receives a license
  8 31 pursuant to this subsection.
  8 32    3.  Notwithstanding subsection 1, beginning January 1,
  8 33 2017, a person who is working in the field of sleep medicine
  8 34 on January 1, 2017, may apply to the board for a license to
  8 35 perform polysomnography. The board shall issue a license to
  9  1 the person, without examination, provided the application
  9  2 contains verification that the person has completed five
  9  3 hundred hours of paid clinical or nonclinical polysomnographic
  9  4 work experience within the three years prior to submission
  9  5 of the application. The application shall also contain
  9  6 verification from the medical director of the person's current
  9  7 employer or the medical director's designee that the person
  9  8 is competent to perform polysomnography. An active license
  9  9 holder under section 147.2 being issued a license under this
  9 10 subsection is exempt from paying the licensure fee required for
  9 11 a polysomnography license.
  9 12    4.  A person who is working in the field of sleep medicine
  9 13 on January 1, 2017, who is not otherwise eligible to obtain
  9 14 a license pursuant to this section shall have until January
  9 15 1, 2018, to achieve a passing score on an examination as
  9 16 designated by the board. The board shall allow the person
  9 17 to attempt the examination and be awarded a license as a
  9 18 polysomnographic technologist by meeting or exceeding the
  9 19 passing point established by the board. After January 1,
  9 20 2018, only persons licensed as polysomnographic technologists
  9 21 pursuant to this chapter, or excepted from the requirements of
  9 22 this chapter may perform sleep=related services.

  7 25 certificate established and accredited by the commission
  7 26 on accreditation of allied health education programs as an
  7 27 extension of the respiratory care program.
  7 28    (2)  Obtaining the sleep disorder specialist credential from
  7 29 the national board for respiratory care.
  7 30    (3)  Obtaining the registered polysomnographic technologist
  7 31 credential from the board of registered polysomnographic
  7 32 technologists.
  7 33    (4)  Completing or obtaining any other certificate or
  7 34 credential program as recognized by the board.
  7 35    c.  Graduation from an electroneurodiagnostic technologist
  8  1 educational program that is accredited by the committee
  8  2 on accreditation for education in electroneurodiagnostic
  8  3 technology or by a committee on accreditation for the
  8  4 commission on accreditation of allied health education
  8  5 programs, and completion of the curriculum for a
  8  6 polysomnographic certificate established and accredited by the
  8  7 commission on accreditation of allied health education programs
  8  8 as an extension of the electroneurodiagnostic educational
  8  9 program.
  8 10    2.  a.  Notwithstanding subsection 1, beginning January
  8 11 1, 2017, the board shall issue a license to perform
  8 12 polysomnography to an individual who holds an active license
  8 13 under section 147.2 in a profession other than polysomnography
  8 14 and who is in good standing with the board for that profession
  8 15 upon application to the board demonstrating any of the
  8 16 following:
  8 17    (1)  Successful completion of an educational program in
  8 18 polysomnography approved by the board.
  8 19    (2)  Successful completion of an examination in
  8 20 polysomnography approved by the board.
  8 21    (3)  Verification from the medical director of the
  8 22 individual's current employer or the medical director's
  8 23 designee that the individual has completed on=the=job
  8 24 training in the field of polysomnography as approved by
  8 25 the board, along with written verification from the medical
  8 26 director of the individual's current employer or the medical
  8 27 director's designee that the individual is competent to perform
  8 28 polysomnography.
  8 29    b.  The board shall not collect a licensing or application
  8 30 fee from a health care practitioner who receives a license
  8 31 pursuant to this subsection.
  8 32    3.  Notwithstanding subsection 1, beginning January 1,
  8 33 2017, a person who is working in the field of sleep medicine
  8 34 on January 1, 2017, may apply to the board for a license to
  8 35 perform polysomnography. The board shall issue a license to
  9  1 the person, without examination, provided the application
  9  2 contains verification that the person has completed five
  9  3 hundred hours of paid clinical or nonclinical polysomnographic
  9  4 work experience within the three years prior to submission
  9  5 of the application. The application shall also contain
  9  6 verification from the medical director of the person's current
  9  7 employer or the medical director's designee that the person
  9  8 is competent to perform polysomnography. An active license
  9  9 holder under section 147.2 being issued a license under this
  9 10 subsection is exempt from paying the licensure fee required for
  9 11 a polysomnography license.
  9 12    4.  A person who is working in the field of sleep medicine
  9 13 on January 1, 2017, who is not otherwise eligible to obtain
  9 14 a license pursuant to this section shall have until January
  9 15 1, 2018, to achieve a passing score on an examination as
  9 16 designated by the board. The board shall allow the person
  9 17 to attempt the examination and be awarded a license as a
  9 18 polysomnographic technologist by meeting or exceeding the
  9 19 passing point established by the board. After January 1,
  9 20 2018, only persons licensed as polysomnographic technologists
  9 21 pursuant to this chapter, or excepted from the requirements of
  9 22 this chapter may perform sleep=related services.
  9 23    5.  The fees assessed by the board shall be sufficient to
  9 24 cover all costs associated with the administration of this
  9 25 chapter.

  9  9 holder under section 147.2 being issued a license under this
  9 10 subsection is exempt from paying the licensure fee required for
  9 11 a polysomnography license.
  9 12    4.  A person who is working in the field of sleep medicine
  9 13 on January 1, 2017, who is not otherwise eligible to obtain
  9 14 a license pursuant to this section shall have until January
  9 15 1, 2018, to achieve a passing score on an examination as
  9 16 designated by the board. The board shall allow the person
  9 17 to attempt the examination and be awarded a license as a
  9 18 polysomnographic technologist by meeting or exceeding the
  9 19 passing point established by the board. After January 1,
  9 20 2018, only persons licensed as polysomnographic technologists
  9 21 pursuant to this chapter, or excepted from the requirements of
  9 22 this chapter may perform sleep=related services.
  9 23    5.  The fees assessed by the board shall be sufficient to
  9 24 cover all costs associated with the administration of this
  9 25 chapter.

  7 23 programs, and any of the following:

  7 30    (3)  Obtaining the registered polysomnographic technologist
  7 31 credential from the board of registered polysomnographic
  7 32 technologists.
  7 33    (4)  Completing or obtaining any other certificate or
  7 34 credential program as recognized by the board.
  7 35    c.  Graduation from an electroneurodiagnostic technologist
  8  1 educational program that is accredited by the committee
  8  2 on accreditation for education in electroneurodiagnostic
  8  3 technology or by a committee on accreditation for the
  8  4 commission on accreditation of allied health education
  8  5 programs, and completion of the curriculum for a
  8  6 polysomnographic certificate established and accredited by the
  8  7 commission on accreditation of allied health education programs
  8  8 as an extension of the electroneurodiagnostic educational
  8  9 program.
  8 10    2.  a.  Notwithstanding subsection 1, beginning January
  8 11 1, 2017, the board shall issue a license to perform
  8 12 polysomnography to an individual who holds an active license
  8 13 under section 147.2 in a profession other than polysomnography
  8 14 and who is in good standing with the board for that profession
  8 15 upon application to the board demonstrating any of the
  8 16 following:
  8 17    (1)  Successful completion of an educational program in
  8 18 polysomnography approved by the board.
  8 19    (2)  Successful completion of an examination in
  8 20 polysomnography approved by the board.
  8 21    (3)  Verification from the medical director of the
  8 22 individual's current employer or the medical director's
  8 23 designee that the individual has completed on=the=job
  8 24 training in the field of polysomnography as approved by
  8 25 the board, along with written verification from the medical
  8 26 director of the individual's current employer or the medical
  8 27 director's designee that the individual is competent to perform
  8 28 polysomnography.
  8 29    b.  The board shall not collect a licensing or application
  8 30 fee from a health care practitioner who receives a license
  8 31 pursuant to this subsection.
  8 32    3.  Notwithstanding subsection 1, beginning January 1,
  8 33 2017, a person who is working in the field of sleep medicine
  8 34 on January 1, 2017, may apply to the board for a license to
  8 35 perform polysomnography. The board shall issue a license to
  9  1 the person, without examination, provided the application
  9  2 contains verification that the person has completed five
  9  3 hundred hours of paid clinical or nonclinical polysomnographic
  9  4 work experience within the three years prior to submission
  9  5 of the application. The application shall also contain
  9  6 verification from the medical director of the person's current
  9  7 employer or the medical director's designee that the person
  9  8 is competent to perform polysomnography. An active license
  9  9 holder under section 147.2 being issued a license under this
  9 10 subsection is exempt from paying the licensure fee required for
  9 11 a polysomnography license.
  9 12    4.  A person who is working in the field of sleep medicine
  9 13 on January 1, 2017, who is not otherwise eligible to obtain
  9 14 a license pursuant to this section shall have until January
  9 15 1, 2018, to achieve a passing score on an examination as
  9 16 designated by the board. The board shall allow the person
  9 17 to attempt the examination and be awarded a license as a
  9 18 polysomnographic technologist by meeting or exceeding the
  9 19 passing point established by the board. After January 1,
  9 20 2018, only persons licensed as polysomnographic technologists
  9 21 pursuant to this chapter, or excepted from the requirements of
  9 22 this chapter may perform sleep=related services.
  9 23    5.  The fees assessed by the board shall be sufficient to
  9 24 cover all costs associated with the administration of this
  9 25 chapter.

  8 10    2.  a.  Notwithstanding subsection 1, beginning January
  8 11 1, 2017, the board shall issue a license to perform
  8 12 polysomnography to an individual who holds an active license
  8 13 under section 147.2 in a profession other than polysomnography
  8 14 and who is in good standing with the board for that profession
  8 15 upon application to the board demonstrating any of the
  8 16 following:
  8 17    (1)  Successful completion of an educational program in
  8 18 polysomnography approved by the board.
  8 19    (2)  Successful completion of an examination in
  8 20 polysomnography approved by the board.
  8 21    (3)  Verification from the medical director of the
  8 22 individual's current employer or the medical director's
  8 23 designee that the individual has completed on=the=job
  8 24 training in the field of polysomnography as approved by
  8 25 the board, along with written verification from the medical
  8 26 director of the individual's current employer or the medical
  8 27 director's designee that the individual is competent to perform
  8 28 polysomnography.
  8 29    b.  The board shall not collect a licensing or application
  8 30 fee from a health care practitioner who receives a license
  8 31 pursuant to this subsection.
  8 32    3.  Notwithstanding subsection 1, beginning January 1,
  8 33 2017, a person who is working in the field of sleep medicine
  8 34 on January 1, 2017, may apply to the board for a license to
  8 35 perform polysomnography. The board shall issue a license to
  9  1 the person, without examination, provided the application
  9  2 contains verification that the person has completed five
  9  3 hundred hours of paid clinical or nonclinical polysomnographic
  9  4 work experience within the three years prior to submission
  9  5 of the application. The application shall also contain
  9  6 verification from the medical director of the person's current
  9  7 employer or the medical director's designee that the person
  9  8 is competent to perform polysomnography. An active license
  9  9 holder under section 147.2 being issued a license under this
  9 10 subsection is exempt from paying the licensure fee required for
  9 11 a polysomnography license.
  9 12    4.  A person who is working in the field of sleep medicine
  9 13 on January 1, 2017, who is not otherwise eligible to obtain
  9 14 a license pursuant to this section shall have until January
  9 15 1, 2018, to achieve a passing score on an examination as
  9 16 designated by the board. The board shall allow the person
  9 17 to attempt the examination and be awarded a license as a
  9 18 polysomnographic technologist by meeting or exceeding the
  9 19 passing point established by the board. After January 1,
  9 20 2018, only persons licensed as polysomnographic technologists
  9 21 pursuant to this chapter, or excepted from the requirements of
  9 22 this chapter may perform sleep=related services.
  9 23    5.  The fees assessed by the board shall be sufficient to
  9 24 cover all costs associated with the administration of this
  9 25 chapter.

  9  3 hundred hours of paid clinical or nonclinical polysomnographic
  9  4 work experience within the three years prior to submission
  9  5 of the application. The application shall also contain
  9  6 verification from the medical director of the person's current
  9  7 employer or the medical director's designee that the person
  9  8 is competent to perform polysomnography. An active license
  9  9 holder under section 147.2 being issued a license under this
  9 10 subsection is exempt from paying the licensure fee required for
  9 11 a polysomnography license.
  9 12    4.  A person who is working in the field of sleep medicine
  9 13 on January 1, 2017, who is not otherwise eligible to obtain
  9 14 a license pursuant to this section shall have until January
  9 15 1, 2018, to achieve a passing score on an examination as
  9 16 designated by the board. The board shall allow the person
  9 17 to attempt the examination and be awarded a license as a
  9 18 polysomnographic technologist by meeting or exceeding the
  9 19 passing point established by the board. After January 1,
  9 20 2018, only persons licensed as polysomnographic technologists
  9 21 pursuant to this chapter, or excepted from the requirements of
  9 22 this chapter may perform sleep=related services.
  9 23    5.  The fees assessed by the board shall be sufficient to
  9 24 cover all costs associated with the administration of this
  9 25 chapter.
  9 26    Sec. 13.    8 12 polysomnography to an individual who holds an active license

  8 23 designee that the individual has completed on=the=job

  8 25 the board, along with written verification from the medical
  8 26 director of the individual's current employer or the medical
  8 27 director's designee that the individual is competent to perform
  8 28 polysomnography.

  8 31 pursuant to this subsection.

  8 26 director of the individual's current employer or the medical
  8 27 director's designee that the individual is competent to perform
  8 28 polysomnography.
  8 29    b.  The board shall not collect a licensing or application
  8 30 fee from a health care practitioner who receives a license
  8 31 pursuant to this subsection.
  8 32    3.  Notwithstanding subsection 1, beginning January 1,
  8 33 2017, a person who is working in the field of sleep medicine
  8 34 on January 1, 2017, may apply to the board for a license to
  8 35 perform polysomnography. The board shall issue a license to
  9  1 the person, without examination, provided the application
  9  2 contains verification that the person has completed five
  9  3 hundred hours of paid clinical or nonclinical polysomnographic
  9  4 work experience within the three years prior to submission
  9  5 of the application. The application shall also contain
  9  6 verification from the medical director of the person's current
  9  7 employer or the medical director's designee that the person
  9  8 is competent to perform polysomnography. An active license
  9  9 holder under section 147.2 being issued a license under this
  9 10 subsection is exempt from paying the licensure fee required for
  9 11 a polysomnography license.
  9 12    4.  A person who is working in the field of sleep medicine
  9 13 on January 1, 2017, who is not otherwise eligible to obtain
  9 14 a license pursuant to this section shall have until January
  9 15 1, 2018, to achieve a passing score on an examination as
  9 16 designated by the board. The board shall allow the person
  9 17 to attempt the examination and be awarded a license as a
  9 18 polysomnographic technologist by meeting or exceeding the
  9 19 passing point established by the board. After January 1,
  9 20 2018, only persons licensed as polysomnographic technologists
  9 21 pursuant to this chapter, or excepted from the requirements of
  9 22 this chapter may perform sleep=related services.
  9 23    5.  The fees assessed by the board shall be sufficient to
  9 24 cover all costs associated with the administration of this
  9 25 chapter.

  9 26    Sec. 13.    9 26    Sec. 13.    9 27 requirement.
  9 28    1.  The following persons may provide sleep=related services
  9 29 without being licensed as a polysomnographic technologist under
  9 30 this chapter:
  9 31    a.  A qualified health care practitioner may provide
  9 32 sleep=related services under the direct supervision of a
  9 33 licensed polysomnographic technologist for a period of up to
  9 34 six months while gaining the clinical experience necessary
  9 35 to meet the admission requirements for a polysomnographic
 10  1 credentialing examination. The board may grant a one=time
 10  2 extension of up to six months.
 10  3    b.  A polysomnographic student may provide sleep=related
 10  4 services under the direct supervision of a polysomnographic
 10  5 technologist as a part of the student's educational program
 10  6 while actively enrolled in a polysomnographic educational
 10  7 program that is accredited by the commission on accreditation
 10  8 of allied health education programs or an equivalent program as
 10  9 determined by the board.
 10 10    2.  Before providing any sleep=related services, a
 10 11 polysomnographic technician or polysomnographic student who is
 10 12 obtaining clinical experience shall give notice to the board
 10 13 that the person is working under the direct supervision of a
 10 14 polysomnographic technologist in order to gain the experience
 10 15 to be eligible to sit for a national certification examination.
 10 16 The person shall wear a badge that appropriately identifies the
 10 17 person while providing such services.

 10 29 152B  10 29 152B  10 30 148G 10 31    Sec. 17.  INITIAL APPOINTMENT OF POLYSOMNOGRAPHIC
 10 32 TECHNOLOGIST TO BOARD.  For the initial appointment of the
 10 33 polysomnographic member to the board of respiratory care and
 10 34 polysomnography pursuant to section 147.14, as amended in this
 10 35 Act, such appointee must be eligible for licensure pursuant to
 11  1 this Act. The appointment shall be effective upon the first
 11  2 expiration of the term of an existing respiratory care board
 11  3 member which occurs after the effective date of this section
 11  4 of this Act.
 11  5    Sec. 18.  EFFECTIVE DATE.  The following provision or
 11  6 provisions of this Act take effect January 1, 2017:
 11  7    1.  The section of this Act amending section 147.2,
 11  8 subsection 1.
 11  9                           EXPLANATION
 11 10 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
 11 11 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
 11 12    This bill requires the licensing of polysomnographic
 11 13 technologists beginning January 1, 2017, and makes the
 11 14 provisions of Code chapters 147 and 272C, including penalty
 11 15 and other regulatory provisions, applicable to other health
 11 16 professions applicable to the practice of polysomnography.
 11 17 Code section 147.86 provides that it is a serious misdemeanor
 11 18 to violate a provision of the licensing laws. A serious
 11 19 misdemeanor is punishable by confinement for no more than one
 11 20 year and a fine of at least $315 but not more than $1,875. The
 11 21 licensing program is administered and regulated by the board of
 11 22 respiratory care and polysomnography, with one respiratory care
 11 23 practitioner replaced by a polysomnographic technologist.
 11 24    The bill provides that the board may issue a license to
 11 25 a person who has graduated from one of three educational
 11 26 programs approved by the board. If the educational program
 11 27 was in respiratory care, the person must also have received a
 11 28 certification or credential as a sleep disorder specialist,
 11 29 a registered polysomnographic technologist, or other area as
 11 30 designated by the board. The board shall also issue a license
 11 31 to practice polysomnography to any individual licensed under
 11 32 Code section 147.2 as long as the individual shows the board
 11 33 that the individual has completed an educational program
 11 34 or passed an examination approved by the board or receives
 11 35 verification from the medical director of the individual's
 12  1 current employer that the individual has completed on=the=job
 12  2 training and is competent to perform polysomnography. The
 12  3 board shall license a person working in the field of sleep
 12  4 medicine on January 1, 2017, without examination, to perform
 12  5 polysomnography. The applicant must provide evidence that
 12  6 the applicant has completed 500 hours of paid clinical or
 12  7 nonclinical polysomnographic work experience within the
 12  8 three years prior to submission of the application. The
 12  9 application shall also contain verification from the medical
 12 10 director of the person's current employer that the applicant
 12 11 is competent to perform polysomnography. A person currently
 12 12 practicing polysomnography who is not otherwise eligible for
 12 13 licensure under the bill has until January 1, 2018, to pass an
 12 14 examination approved by the board.
 12 15    An active license holder under Code section 147.2 being
 12 16 issued a license under the bill is exempt from paying the
 12 17 licensure fee required for a polysomnography license. The fees
 12 18 assessed by the board shall be sufficient to cover all costs
 12 19 associated with the administration of the bill.
 12 20    A licensed polysomnographic technologist practices under
 12 21 the general supervision of a physician, a physician assistant,
 12 22 or an advanced registered nurse practitioner, providing
 12 23 specifically enumerated services related to sleep disorders. A
 12 24 polysomnographic student enrolled in an approved educational
 12 25 program provides services under the direct supervision of a
 12 26 polysomnographic technologist.
       LSB 1669SV (3) 86
       tr/nh

       LSB 1669SV (3) 86
       tr/nh
 11  3 member which occurs after the effective date of this section
 11  4 of this Act.
 11  5    Sec. 18.  EFFECTIVE DATE.  The following provision or
 11  6 provisions of this Act take effect January 1, 2017:
 11  7    1.  The section of this Act amending section 147.2,
 11  8 subsection 1.
 11  9                           EXPLANATION
 11 10 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
 11 11 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
 11 12    This bill requires the licensing of polysomnographic
 11 13 technologists beginning January 1, 2017, and makes the
 11 14 provisions of Code chapters 147 and 272C, including penalty
 11 15 and other regulatory provisions, applicable to other health
 11 16 professions applicable to the practice of polysomnography.
 11 17 Code section 147.86 provides that it is a serious misdemeanor
 11 18 to violate a provision of the licensing laws. A serious
 11 19 misdemeanor is punishable by confinement for no more than one
 11 20 year and a fine of at least $315 but not more than $1,875. The
 11 21 licensing program is administered and regulated by the board of
 11 22 respiratory care and polysomnography, with one respiratory care
 11 23 practitioner replaced by a polysomnographic technologist.
 11 24    The bill provides that the board may issue a license to
 11 25 a person who has graduated from one of three educational
 11 26 programs approved by the board. If the educational program
 11 27 was in respiratory care, the person must also have received a
 11 28 certification or credential as a sleep disorder specialist,
 11 29 a registered polysomnographic technologist, or other area as
 11 30 designated by the board. The board shall also issue a license
 11 31 to practice polysomnography to any individual licensed under
 11 32 Code section 147.2 as long as the individual shows the board
 11 33 that the individual has completed an educational program
 11 34 or passed an examination approved by the board or receives
 11 35 verification from the medical director of the individual's
 12  1 current employer that the individual has completed on=the=job
 12  2 training and is competent to perform polysomnography. The
 12  3 board shall license a person working in the field of sleep
 12  4 medicine on January 1, 2017, without examination, to perform
 12  5 polysomnography. The applicant must provide evidence that
 12  6 the applicant has completed 500 hours of paid clinical or
 12  7 nonclinical polysomnographic work experience within the
 12  8 three years prior to submission of the application. The
 12  9 application shall also contain verification from the medical
 12 10 director of the person's current employer that the applicant
 12 11 is competent to perform polysomnography. A person currently
 12 12 practicing polysomnography who is not otherwise eligible for
 12 13 licensure under the bill has until January 1, 2018, to pass an
 12 14 examination approved by the board.
 12 15    An active license holder under Code section 147.2 being
 12 16 issued a license under the bill is exempt from paying the
 12 17 licensure fee required for a polysomnography license. The fees
 12 18 assessed by the board shall be sufficient to cover all costs
 12 19 associated with the administration of the bill.
 12 20    A licensed polysomnographic technologist practices under
 12 21 the general supervision of a physician, a physician assistant,
 12 22 or an advanced registered nurse practitioner, providing
 12 23 specifically enumerated services related to sleep disorders. A
 12 24 polysomnographic student enrolled in an approved educational
 12 25 program provides services under the direct supervision of a
 12 26 polysomnographic technologist.
       LSB 1669SV (3) 86
       tr/nh
 11  4 of this Act.

 12 16 issued a license under the bill is exempt from paying the
 12 17 licensure fee required for a polysomnography license. The fees
 12 18 assessed by the board shall be sufficient to cover all costs
 12 19 associated with the administration of the bill.
 12 20    A licensed polysomnographic technologist practices under
 12 21 the general supervision of a physician, a physician assistant,
 12 22 or an advanced registered nurse practitioner, providing
 12 23 specifically enumerated services related to sleep disorders. A
 12 24 polysomnographic student enrolled in an approved educational
 12 25 program provides services under the direct supervision of a
 12 26 polysomnographic technologist.
       LSB 1669SV (3) 86
       tr/nh
 11 13 technologists beginning January 1, 2017, and makes the
 11 14 provisions of Code chapters 147 and 272C, including penalty
 11 15 and other regulatory provisions, applicable to other health
 11 16 professions applicable to the practice of polysomnography.
 11 17 Code section 147.86 provides that it is a serious misdemeanor
 11 18 to violate a provision of the licensing laws. A serious
 11 19 misdemeanor is punishable by confinement for no more than one
 11 20 year and a fine of at least $315 but not more than $1,875. The
 11 21 licensing program is administered and regulated by the board of
 11 22 respiratory care and polysomnography, with one respiratory care
 11 23 practitioner replaced by a polysomnographic technologist.
 11 24    The bill provides that the board may issue a license to
 11 25 a person who has graduated from one of three educational
 11 26 programs approved by the board. If the educational program
 11 27 was in respiratory care, the person must also have received a
 11 28 certification or credential as a sleep disorder specialist,
 11 29 a registered polysomnographic technologist, or other area as
 11 30 designated by the board. The board shall also issue a license
 11 31 to practice polysomnography to any individual licensed under
 11 32 Code section 147.2 as long as the individual shows the board
 11 33 that the individual has completed an educational program
 11 34 or passed an examination approved by the board or receives
 11 35 verification from the medical director of the individual's
 12  1 current employer that the individual has completed on=the=job
 12  2 training and is competent to perform polysomnography. The
 12  3 board shall license a person working in the field of sleep
 12  4 medicine on January 1, 2017, without examination, to perform
 12  5 polysomnography. The applicant must provide evidence that
 12  6 the applicant has completed 500 hours of paid clinical or
 12  7 nonclinical polysomnographic work experience within the
 12  8 three years prior to submission of the application. The
 12  9 application shall also contain verification from the medical
 12 10 director of the person's current employer that the applicant
 12 11 is competent to perform polysomnography. A person currently
 12 12 practicing polysomnography who is not otherwise eligible for
 12 13 licensure under the bill has until January 1, 2018, to pass an
 12 14 examination approved by the board.
 12 15    An active license holder under Code section 147.2 being
 12 16 issued a license under the bill is exempt from paying the
 12 17 licensure fee required for a polysomnography license. The fees
 12 18 assessed by the board shall be sufficient to cover all costs

 12 26 polysomnographic technologist.
       LSB 1669SV (3) 86
       tr/nh
 11 25 a person who has graduated from one of three educational
 11 26 programs approved by the board. If the educational program
 11 27 was in respiratory care, the person must also have received a
 11 28 certification or credential as a sleep disorder specialist,
 11 29 a registered polysomnographic technologist, or other area as
 11 30 designated by the board. The board shall also issue a license
 11 31 to practice polysomnography to any individual licensed under
 11 32 Code section 147.2 as long as the individual shows the board
 11 33 that the individual has completed an educational program
 11 34 or passed an examination approved by the board or receives
 11 35 verification from the medical director of the individual's
 12  1 current employer that the individual has completed on=the=job
 12  2 training and is competent to perform polysomnography. The
 12  3 board shall license a person working in the field of sleep
 12  4 medicine on January 1, 2017, without examination, to perform
 12  5 polysomnography. The applicant must provide evidence that
 12  6 the applicant has completed 500 hours of paid clinical or
 12  7 nonclinical polysomnographic work experience within the
 12  8 three years prior to submission of the application. The
 12  9 application shall also contain verification from the medical
 12 10 director of the person's current employer that the applicant
 12 11 is competent to perform polysomnography. A person currently
 12 12 practicing polysomnography who is not otherwise eligible for
 12 13 licensure under the bill has until January 1, 2018, to pass an
 12 14 examination approved by the board.

 12 16 issued a license under the bill is exempt from paying the
 12 17 licensure fee required for a polysomnography license. The fees
 12 18 assessed by the board shall be sufficient to cover all costs
 12 19 associated with the administration of the bill.

 12  9 application shall also contain verification from the medical
 12 10 director of the person's current employer that the applicant
 12 11 is competent to perform polysomnography. A person currently
 12 12 practicing polysomnography who is not otherwise eligible for
 12 13 licensure under the bill has until January 1, 2018, to pass an
 12 14 examination approved by the board.
 12 15    An active license holder under Code section 147.2 being
 12 16 issued a license under the bill is exempt from paying the
 12 17 licensure fee required for a polysomnography license. The fees
 12 18 assessed by the board shall be sufficient to cover all costs
 12 19 associated with the administration of the bill.
 12 20    A licensed polysomnographic technologist practices under
 12 21 the general supervision of a physician, a physician assistant,
 12 22 or an advanced registered nurse practitioner, providing
 12 23 specifically enumerated services related to sleep disorders. A
 12 24 polysomnographic student enrolled in an approved educational
 12 25 program provides services under the direct supervision of a
 12 26 polysomnographic technologist.
